        </div><div class="casAbstract">A sym. sodium-ion battery with an aq. electrolyte is demonstrated; it utilizes the NASICON-structured Na3MnTi(PO4)3 as both the anode and the cathode.  The NASICON-structured Na3MnTi(PO4)3 possesses two electrochem. active transition metals with the redox couples of Ti4+/Ti3+ and Mn3+/Mn2+ working on the anode and cathode sides, resp.  The sym. cell based on this bipolar electrode material exhibits a well-defined voltage plateau centered at about 1.4 V in an aq. electrolyte with a stable cycle performance and superior rate capability.  The advent of aq. sym. sodium-ion battery with high safety and low cost may provide a soln. for large-scale stationary energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201800194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vieira Carvalho, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Buchholz, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Towards High-Performance Aqueous Sodium-Ion Batteries: Stabilizing the Solid/Liquid Interface for NASICON-Type Na<sub>2</sub>VTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> using Concentrated Electrolytes</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1382</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1389</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Energy Aqueous Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Ting; Ji, Xiao; Wang, Peng-Fei; Zhu, Kunjie; Zhang, Jiaxun; Cao, Longsheng; Chen, Long; Cui, Chunyu; Deng, Tao; Liu, Sufu; Piao, Nan; Liu, Yongchang; Shen, Chao; Xie, Keyu; Jiao, Lifang; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">60</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11943-11948</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Water-in-salt electrolytes (WISE) have largely widened the electrochem. stability window (ESW) of aq. electrolytes by formation of passivating solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) on anode and also absorption of the hydrophobic anion-rich double layer on cathode.  However, the cathodic limiting potential of WISE is still too high for most high-capacity anodes in aq. sodium-ion batteries (ASIBs), and the cost of WISE is also too high for practical application.  Herein, a low-cost 19 m (m: mol kg-1) bi-salts WISE with a wide ESW of 2.8 V was designed, where the low-cost 17 m NaClO4 extends the anodic limiting potential to 4.4 V, while the fluorine-contg. salt (2 m NaOTF) extends the cathodic limiting potential to 1.6 V by forming the NaF-Na2O-NaOH SEI on anode.  The 19 m NaClO4-NaOTF-H2O electrolyte enables a 1.75 V Na3V2(PO4)3||Na3V2(PO4)3 full cell to deliver an appreciable energy d. of 70 Wh kg-1 at 1 C with a capacity retention of 87.5% after 100 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202104053"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multi-functional Flexible Aqueous Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Safety</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Zhaowei; Zhao, Yang; Ding, Yuxue; Dong, Xiaoli; Chen, Long; Cao, Jingyu; Wang, Changchun; Xia, Yongyao; Peng, Huisheng; Wang, Yonggang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">348-362</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMVE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2451-9294</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible energy storage devices are attracting extensive attention, but most of the reported flexible batteries and supercapacitors use either strong acid or base or toxic flammable org. solns. as electrolytes, which pose potential safety issues when worn by humans or implanted into the body.  Here, we present a highly safe family of flexible sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) based on a Na0.44MnO2 cathode, a nano-sized NaTi2(PO4)3@C anode, and various aq. electrolytes contg. Na+.  The resulting belt- and fiber-shaped aq. SIBs exhibit high volumetric energy and power d., high flexibility, and long life and thus can be safely applied in wearable electronic devices.  When normal saline or cell-culture medium is used as the electrolyte, these SIBs can still work well, indicating potential application in implantable electronic devices.  The fiber-shaped electrodes in Na+-contg. aq. electrolytes exhibit an electrochem. deoxygenation function, which could be applied in biol. and medical fields.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b00478"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Symmetric Sodium-Ion Capacitor Based on Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> Nanorods for Low-Cost and High-Performance Energy Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1021/acsami.8b00478</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D11689-11698%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26issue%3D14%26author%3DZ.%2BChen%26author%3DT.%2BYuan%26author%3DX.%2BPu%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BAi%26author%3DY.%2BXia%26author%3DY.%2BCao%26title%3DSymmetric%2BSodium-Ion%2BCapacitor%2BBased%2Bon%2BNa0.44MnO2%2BNanorods%2Bfor%2BLow-Cost%2Band%2BHigh-Performance%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.8b00478&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c18772&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.8b00478&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Symmetric Sodium-Ion Capacitor Based on Na0.44MnO2 Nanorods for Low-Cost and High-Performance Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Zhongxue; Yuan, Tianci; Pu, Xiangjun; Yang, Hanxi; Ai, Xinping; Xia, Yongyao; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11689-11698</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Batteries and electrochem. capacitors play very important roles in the portable electronic devices and elec. vehicles and have shown promising potential for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, batteries or capacitors alone cannot meet the energy and power d. requirements because rechargeable batteries have a poor power property, whereas supercapacitors offer limited capacity.  Here, a novel sym. sodium-ion capacitor (NIC) is developed based on low-cost Na0.44MnO2 nanorods.  The Na0.44MnO2 with unique nanoarchitectures and iso-oriented feature offers shortened diffusion path lengths for both electronic and Na+ transport and reduces the stress assocd. with Na+ insertion and extn.  Benefiting from these merits, the sym. device achieves a high power d. of 2432.7 W kg-1, an improved energy d. of 27.9 Wh kg-1, and a capacitance retention of 85.2% over 5000 cycles.  Particularly, the sym. NIC based on Na0.44MnO2 permits repeatedly reverse-polarity characteristics, thus simplifying energy management system and greatly enhancing the safety under abuse condition.  This cost-effective, high-safety, and high-performance sym. NIC can balance the energy and power d. between batteries and capacitors and serve as an elec. power source for future low-maintenance large-scale energy storage systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1007/s42452-020-03607-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nuti, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Spada, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Quinzeni, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Capelli, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Albini, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Galinetto, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bini, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">From Tunnel NMO to Layered Polymorphs Oxides for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>SN Appl.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-birnessite with high capacity and long cycle life for rechargeable aqueous sodium-ion battery cathode electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xueqian; Hou, Zhiguo; Li, Xiaona; Liang, Jianwen; Zhu, Yongchun; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layer structure Na-birnessite (Na-Bir) Na0.58MnO2·0.48H2O was synthesized through a pptn. reaction at room temp. and used as a rechargeable aq. sodium-ion battery (RASIB) cathode material for the 1st time.  As a RASIB cathode material, the layered Na-birnessite manifests a high specific capacity of 80 mA-h/g at 1C without obvious capacity loss after 150 cycles.  After heat treatment of the Na-Bir sample, it can deliver a specific capacity of 79 mA-h/g at 1C but only retains 60% of the initial capacity after 150 cycles.  The XRD anal. of the Na-Bir sample after 150 cycles reveals that the layer structure is retained, while inductively coupled plasma at. emission spectroscopy (ICP-AES) indicates that the dissoln. of Mn is merely 0.008% of Na-Bir after 150 cycles.  As a cathode electrode in full batteries coupled with a NaTi2(PO4)3 anode electrode, a high capacity of 39 mA h/g at 10C is obtained with a capacity retention of 94% after 1000 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.03.007"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A High Rate 1.2 V Aqueous Sodium-Ion Battery Based on All NASICON Structured NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub></span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High Rate 1.2 V Aqueous Sodium-ion Battery Based on All NASICON Structured NaTi2(PO4)3 and Na3V2(PO4)3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Qing; Liao, Chaoyi; Zhai, Tianyou; Li, Huiqiao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">196</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new aq. rechargeable Na-ion battery is developed based on all NASICON structured electrodes in which NaTi2(PO4)3 serves as the anode, Na3V2(PO4)3 serves as the cathode, and aq. Na2SO4 soln. serves as the electrolyte.  Such a combination of cathode-anode can fulfil the theor. working window of aq. electrolyte, thus give rise to a high cell voltage surpassing most of the previous aq. Na-ion batteries.  The developed NaTi2(PO4)3/Na3V2(PO4)3 aq. full cell demonstrates a flat discharge plateau at 1.2 V and can well maintain its performance at high current rates.  Even at a c.d. of 10 A g-1, the battery discharge capacity can still reach 58 mAh g-1.  Together with a high voltage, this cell configuration enables a high energy d. of 29 Wh kg-1 at a power d. of 5145 W kg-1.  The NaTi2(PO4)3/Na3V2(PO4)3 system can be a promising low cost alternative for the current aq. secondary batteries esp. in terms of the high voltage and high power application.  By controlling the cut-off voltage and adjusting the mass ratio of cathode to anode, the authors explored the different electrochem. performances of the aq. full cell and identify which side of the electrode dominantly affects the cell decay at the case of full using one electrode material.  This study may present useful insight to researchers working on both aq. batteries and NASICON-based materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.7b00623"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kühnel, R.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reber, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Battaglia, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A High-Voltage Aqueous Electrolyte for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Energy Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">9</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2005</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2006</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Computed Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barriers and electronic structure of Na<sub>0.66</sub>[Mn<sub>0.33</sub>Fe<sub>0.33</sub>Ti<sub>0.3</sub>Sn<sub>0.04</sub>]O<sub>2</sub>.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries as a power source are dominating in portable electronics, penetrating the elec. vehicle market, and on the verge of entering the utility market for grid-energy storage.  Depending on the application, trade-offs among the various performance parameters-energy, power, cycle life, cost, safety, and environmental impact-are often needed, which are linked to severe materials chem. challenges.  The current lithium ion battery technol. is based on insertion-reaction electrodes and org. liq. electrolytes.  With an aim to increase the energy d. or optimize the other performance parameters, new electrode materials based on both insertion reaction and dominantly conversion reaction along with solid electrolytes and lithium metal anode are being intensively pursued.  This article presents an outlook on lithium ion technol. by providing first the current status and then the progress and challenges with the ongoing approaches.  In light of the formidable challenges with some of the approaches, the article finally points out practically viable near-term strategies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-020-19991-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Grey, C.                         rightTab-cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage issue of aqueous rechargeable metal-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhuoxin; Huang, Yan; Huang, Yang; Yang, Qi; Li, Xinliang; Huang, Zhaodong; Zhi, Chunyi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">180-232</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Over the past two decades, a series of aq. rechargeable metal-ion batteries (ARMBs) have been developed, aiming at improving safety, environmental friendliness and cost-efficiency in fields of consumer electronics, elec. vehicles and grid-scale energy storage.  However, the notable gap between ARMBs and their org. counterparts in energy d. directly hinders their practical applications, making it difficult to replace current widely-used org. lithium-ion batteries.  Basically, this huge gap in energy d. originates from cell voltage, as the narrow electrochem. stability window of aq. electrolytes substantially confines the choice of electrode materials.  This review highlights various ARMBs with focuses on their voltage characteristics and strategies that can effectively raise battery voltage.  It begins with the discussion on the fundamental factor that limits the voltage of ARMBs, i.e., electrochem. stability window of aq. electrolytes, which decides the max.-allowed p.d. between cathode and anode.  The following section introduces various ARMB systems and compares their voltage characteristics in midpoint voltage and plateau voltage, in relation to resp. electrode materials.  Subsequently, various strategies paving the way to high-voltage ARMBs are summarized, with corresponding advancements highlighted.  The final section presents potential directions for further improvements and future perspectives of this thriving field.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2023.02.001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Regulating the Local Chemical Environment in Layered O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 Achieves Practicable Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>56</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">631</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">641</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Birnessite is a low-cost and environmentally friendly layered material for aqueous electrochemical energy storage; however, its storage capacity is poor due to its narrow potential window in aqueous electrolyte and low redox activity.  Herein we report a sodium rich disordered birnessite (Na0.27MnO2) for aqueous sodium-ion electrochemical storage with a much-enhanced capacity and cycling life (83 mAh g(-1) after 5000 cycles in full-cell).  Neutron total scattering and in situ X-ray diffraction measurements show that both structural water and the Na-rich disordered structure contribute to the improved electrochemical performance of current cathode material.  Particularly, the co-deintercalation of the hydrated water and sodium-ion during the high potential charging process results in the shrinkage of interlayer distance and thus stabilizes the layered structure.  Our results provide a genuine insight into how structural disordering and structural water improve sodium-ion storage in a layered electrode and open up an exciting direction for improving aqueous batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202300334"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahmad, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in the Emerging Modification Strategies for Layered Oxide Cathodes toward Practicable Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Progress in the Emerging Modification Strategies for Layered Oxide Cathodes toward Practicable Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Bo; Wan, Guanglin; Ahmad, Nazir; Yu, Lai; Ma, Xinyi; Zhang, Genqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Low-cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been extensively considered as a supplement or even a replacement for successful lithium-ion batteries.  However, the practical application of SIBs is limited by their energy d. and cyclic performance, which are mainly constrained by the cathode side.  Therefore, the development of advanced cathode materials is essential for the practical application of SIBs.  Among the various cathode materials, layered transition metal oxides (LTMOs) are highly promising candidates due to their compact crystal structure, low-cost, ease of prepn., and similarities to successful Li-based LTMOs.  Unfortunately, the bottleneck issues faced by Na-based LTMOs, such as severe phase transitions, sluggish diffusion kinetics, and interface deterioration, pose significant challenges in achieving high-performance cathodes.  In this review, a comprehensive overview and summary of recently reported modification strategies for layered oxides are provided and the structure-function-performance relationship is refined.  A perspective on the outlook and development direction for Na-based LTMOs cathodes is also provided.  This review comprehensively explores the modification strategies of Na-based LTMOs, providing a new horizon for future research on Na-based LTMOs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms4007"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pasta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wessells, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">H2O-in-salt (WiS) electrolytes provide a new pathway to widen the electrochem. window of aq. electrolytes.  However, their formulation strongly depends on the soly. of the chosen salts, imposing a stringent restriction on the no. of possible WiS systems.  This issue becomes more severe for aq. Na-ion batteries (ANIBs) owing to the relatively lower soly. of Na salts compared to its alk. cousins (Li, K, and Cs).  A new class of the inert-cation-assisted WiS (IC-WiS) electrolytes contg. the Et4N+ (TEA+) inert cation is reported.  The Na IC-WiS electrolyte at a superhigh concn. of 31 mol kg-1 exhibits a wide electrochem. window of 3.3 V, suppresses transition metal dissoln. from the cathode, and ensures singular intercalation of Na into both cathode and anode electrodes during cycling, which is often problematic in mixed alkali cation systems such as K-Na and Li-Na.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible energy storage devices are attracting extensive attention, but most of the reported flexible batteries and supercapacitors use either strong acid or base or toxic flammable org. solns. as electrolytes, which pose potential safety issues when worn by humans or implanted into the body.  Here, we present a highly safe family of flexible sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) based on a Na0.44MnO2 cathode, a nano-sized NaTi2(PO4)3@C anode, and various aq. electrolytes contg. Na+.  The resulting belt- and fiber-shaped aq. SIBs exhibit high volumetric energy and power d., high flexibility, and long life and thus can be safely applied in wearable electronic devices.  When normal saline or cell-culture medium is used as the electrolyte, these SIBs can still work well, indicating potential application in implantable electronic devices.  The fiber-shaped electrodes in Na+-contg. aq. electrolytes exhibit an electrochem. deoxygenation function, which could be applied in biol. and medical fields.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b00478"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Symmetric Sodium-Ion Capacitor Based on Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> Nanorods for Low-Cost and High-Performance Energy Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Batteries and electrochem. capacitors play very important roles in the portable electronic devices and elec. vehicles and have shown promising potential for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, batteries or capacitors alone cannot meet the energy and power d. requirements because rechargeable batteries have a poor power property, whereas supercapacitors offer limited capacity.  Here, a novel sym. sodium-ion capacitor (NIC) is developed based on low-cost Na0.44MnO2 nanorods.  The Na0.44MnO2 with unique nanoarchitectures and iso-oriented feature offers shortened diffusion path lengths for both electronic and Na+ transport and reduces the stress assocd. with Na+ insertion and extn.  Benefiting from these merits, the sym. device achieves a high power d. of 2432.7 W kg-1, an improved energy d. of 27.9 Wh kg-1, and a capacitance retention of 85.2% over 5000 cycles.  Particularly, the sym. NIC based on Na0.44MnO2 permits repeatedly reverse-polarity characteristics, thus simplifying energy management system and greatly enhancing the safety under abuse condition.  This cost-effective, high-safety, and high-performance sym. NIC can balance the energy and power d. between batteries and capacitors and serve as an elec. power source for future low-maintenance large-scale energy storage systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1007/s42452-020-03607-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nuti, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Spada, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Quinzeni, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Capelli, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Albini, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Galinetto, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bini, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">From Tunnel NMO to Layered Polymorphs Oxides for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>SN Appl.                         rightTab-cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-birnessite with high capacity and long cycle life for rechargeable aqueous sodium-ion battery cathode electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xueqian; Hou, Zhiguo; Li, Xiaona; Liang, Jianwen; Zhu, Yongchun; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layer structure Na-birnessite (Na-Bir) Na0.58MnO2·0.48H2O was synthesized through a pptn. reaction at room temp. and used as a rechargeable aq. sodium-ion battery (RASIB) cathode material for the 1st time.  As a RASIB cathode material, the layered Na-birnessite manifests a high specific capacity of 80 mA-h/g at 1C without obvious capacity loss after 150 cycles.  After heat treatment of the Na-Bir sample, it can deliver a specific capacity of 79 mA-h/g at 1C but only retains 60% of the initial capacity after 150 cycles.  The XRD anal. of the Na-Bir sample after 150 cycles reveals that the layer structure is retained, while inductively coupled plasma at. emission spectroscopy (ICP-AES) indicates that the dissoln. of Mn is merely 0.008% of Na-Bir after 150 cycles.  As a cathode electrode in full batteries coupled with a NaTi2(PO4)3 anode electrode, a high capacity of 39 mA h/g at 10C is obtained with a capacity retention of 94% after 1000 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.03.007"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A High Rate 1.2 V Aqueous Sodium-Ion Battery Based on All NASICON Structured NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub></span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>196</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">470</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">478</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2016.03.007</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High Rate 1.2 V Aqueous Sodium-ion Battery Based on All NASICON Structured NaTi2(PO4)3 and Na3V2(PO4)3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Qing; Liao, Chaoyi; Zhai, Tianyou; Li, Huiqiao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">196</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">470-478</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new aq. rechargeable Na-ion battery is developed based on all NASICON structured electrodes in which NaTi2(PO4)3 serves as the anode, Na3V2(PO4)3 serves as the cathode, and aq. Na2SO4 soln. serves as the electrolyte.  Such a combination of cathode-anode can fulfil the theor. working window of aq. electrolyte, thus give rise to a high cell voltage surpassing most of the previous aq. Na-ion batteries.  The developed NaTi2(PO4)3/Na3V2(PO4)3 aq. full cell demonstrates a flat discharge plateau at 1.2 V and can well maintain its performance at high current rates.  Even at a c.d. of 10 A g-1, the battery discharge capacity can still reach 58 mAh g-1.  Together with a high voltage, this cell configuration enables a high energy d. of 29 Wh kg-1 at a power d. of 5145 W kg-1.  The NaTi2(PO4)3/Na3V2(PO4)3 system can be a promising low cost alternative for the current aq. secondary batteries esp. in terms of the high voltage and high power application.  By controlling the cut-off voltage and adjusting the mass ratio of cathode to anode, the authors explored the different electrochem. performances of the aq. full cell and identify which side of the electrode dominantly affects the cell decay at the case of full using one electrode material.  This study may present useful insight to researchers working on both aq. batteries and NASICON-based materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.7b00623"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kühnel, R.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reber, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Battaglia, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A High-Voltage Aqueous Electrolyte for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Energy Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">9</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2005</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2006</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsenergylett.7b00623</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X. Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel High Capacity Positive Electrode Material with Tunnel-Type Structure for Aqueous Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">22</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1501005</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201501005</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i13">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c18772?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c18772</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Detailed experimental section, crystallographic data and powder XRD Rietveld refinement results, SEM images, XRD patterns, CV profiles, Galvanostatic charge–discharge voltage profiles, cycle performances, EIS results, and fitting data of the <sup>57</sup>Fe Mössbauer (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c18772/suppl_file/am4c18772_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c18772/suppl_file/am4c18772_si_001.pdf">am4c18772_si_001.pdf (1.25 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

<script nonce="931886249eed54b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="931886249eed54b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>
-->

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
